## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t), following Newton's second law.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic dissipation)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (Duffing + Van der Pol)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Driven with nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - c3 * x**2) * v + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (full nonlinear driven-damped system)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x²) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Position-velocity coupling terms like v*x² indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type self-oscillation
- Trigonometric functions of time (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) indicate external periodic driving forces
- The sign of the cubic coefficient determines hardening (same sign as linear) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or only exchanged through x-v coupling
- Rational functions of x like x/(1 + c*x²) can model bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements
- Products of trigonometric functions of t with x indicate parametric excitation rather than direct forcing
